REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON ROADS AND BRIDGES
June 9, 2004
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County
ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Hansen, Vice Chairman Moreno, Commissioners Butler, Collins, Daley, Gorman,
Maldonado, Murphy, Steele, Suffredin and Sims (I I)

Absent:

Commissioners Claypool, Goslin, Peraica, Quigley, Silvestri and President Stroger (6)

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Roads and Bridges of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to
notice on Wednesday, June 9, 2004 at the hour of 10:30 A.M . in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois to consider the following.
265630

AMENDMENT TO CHAPTER 11: TRAFFIC REGULATION OF THE COOK COUNTY
ORDINANCES
(PROPOSED
ORDINANCE AMENDMENT/MOTOR
DRlVEN
SCOOTERS). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by Carl R. Hansen,
County Commissioner.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance Amendment:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
AMENDING CHAPTER l l: TRAFFIC REGULATION
OF THE COOK COUNTY ORDINANCES
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article
VII, section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and
perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County has adopted ordinances
governing traffic regulation for the protection of the public health, safety, comfort and
welfare; and

1857

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE I 5, 2004
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County desires to amend the ordinances
governing traffic regulation for the protection of the public health, safety, comfort and
welfare by adding provisions which establish certain limitations on the use of motor driven
scooters on public ways within the County;
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED THAT:
Section 1: Definitions.
Section 2: Operation of Motor Driven Scooters Restricted.
Section 3: Exemptions.
Section 4: Applicability of this Ordinance.
Section 5: Violations.
Section 6: Effective Date.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Murphy moved the incorporation of the following
language: "is defined as any electric vehicle or gas driven wheeled scooter vehicle, motor-driven
cycle or other similar motor-driven vehicle." The motion carried.
The following public speakers spoke:
I.

2.
3.
4.
5.

Richard Eddington - Chief of Police, Mount Prospect
Tom Folliard - Deputy Chief of Patrol, Cook County Sheriff's Police
Eddie McCann, Jr.- First Deputy Chief of Police, Forest Preserve District
Wally Kos - Superintendent, Highway Department
James Beligratis - State's Attorney's Office

Chainnan Hansen noted that Mount Prospect, Elgin, Des Plaines and Hoffman Estates have approved
similar ordinances.
Richard Eddington, Chief of Police, Mount Prospect, stated that motor-driven scooters need to be
regulated because of the low survivability of accidents; no helmet laws govern them. Also, they do not fit
into the existing Jllinois Vehicle Code. Mount Prospect adopted an ordinance prohibiting these scooters
from public roadways and sidewalks.
Commissioner Murphy asked whether there are specific, designated places where the scooters can be
driven, or are they altogether banned.
Chief Eddington replied that they are banned from public roadways and sidewalks.
Commissioner Steele asked whether this ordinance will only impact the unincorporated areas of Cook
County.
Chainnan Hansen noted that a boy of fourteen was killed riding a motorized scooter at the intersection of
Northwest Highway and Mount Prospect Highway.
Commissioner Maldonado asked Chief Eddington how the public has reacted to the ordinance.

1858

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

Chief Eddington replied that the village board encouraged a six month public education campaign, and
that there has been widespread acceptance of the ordinance in the community.
Commissioner Gonnan asked whether there is a helmet requirement under the ordinance and what the
North Suburban Chiefs Association recommended.
Most of the chiefs have adhered to or suggested a motorized scooter ban.
Commissioner Murphy asked how fast the motor scooters can travel.
Chief Eddington replied that they possibly could travel up to 60 mph in some instances.
Commissioner Butler asked whether the sale of motorized scooters was going to be made illegal.
Chief Eddington replied that this was outside of the purview of the Village of Mount Prospect. Also, it is
legal to operate motorized scooters on private property.
Commissioner Butler noted that policemen ride motor scooters.
Chief Eddington replied that they are exempt under the ordinance; there is an experimental police
program at O'Hare. In this controlled environment, such things as pot holes pose no challenge.
Chairman Hansen noted the ordinance exempts the following vehicles driven in the course of duty: police,
fire, municipal, special district, county or forest preserve. He also noted that the City of Chicago code
states the unlawfulness of persons under 16 to operate motorized vehicles not to exceed 5 brake
horsepower.
Commissioner Butler noted that the average person doesn't know about an ordinance until they violate it
and this is unfair.
Commissioner Maldonado stated that he supports the ordinance and that gang-bangers and their younger
siblings ride the scooters in his district.
Commissioner Collins stated that the state should place a ban on motorized scooters.
Commissioner Suffredin asked whether the North Suburban Chiefs Association has taken a position on
this ordinance.
Chief Eddington replied that, based on the advice of counsel, the Association has supported the ordinance.
Commissioner Suffredin asked whether any other counties have passed a similar ordinance.
Chief Eddington replied not to his knowledge.
Commissioner Sims asked whether the ordinance regulates sales to minors.
Chief Eddington replied in the negative. Instead, a six month pubic education campaign was launched
through a newsletter, cable television and media resources. This campaign was run before the Christmas
rush.

1859

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

Commissioner Moreno suggested that notices be put on the motor scooter boxes indicating that the
scooters cannot be used in Cook County.
Chairman Hansen asked whether there is any legal prohibition of the motor scooters under state Jaw.
Chief Eddington replied in the negative.
Chainnan Hansen asked whether there is a state allowance for the presence of motor scooters on the state
roads.
Chief Eddington replied in the negative.
Tom Folliard, Deputy Chief of Patrol, Cook County Sheriffs Police, stated that both the safety of the
motor scooter rider and of pedestrians are issues; in particular there are many complaints by senior
citizens.
Chairman Hansen asked whether these motor scooters pose a danger.
Deputy Chief Folliard, replied in the affinnative, especially on side walks.
Chainnan Hansen noted the difference between a non-motor scooter and a motor scooter, and noted that a
child does not have a sense of perspective on how to operate a motor scooter, and these motor scooters are
particularly dangerous to elderly pedestrians.
Commissioner Steele noted that in her district, adults operate motor scooters while dealing drugs.
Commissioner Daley asked whether the Sheriffs Office wi ll be issuing tickets once the ordinance is
passed and what the policy will be regarding a first offense.
Deputy Chief Folliard stated that instead of starting out with zero tolerance there should be a phased in
infonnational period and a phased in ticketing period. During the infonnational period public meetings
would be held, information would be filtered through the schools, and fl yering would be done. There
should also be a period of infonnational ticketing before punitive ticketing begins.
Chaim1an Hansen asked how long a phase-in period would be required.
Deputy Chief Folliard repl ied that three months should be sufficient.
Chainnan Hansen noted that the ordinance would have to be amended to include a phase-in period.
Commissioner Butler noted that the ordinance would not have any effect in Commissioners Sims and
Steele's districts.
Chainnan Hansen made the distinction that the policy of the City of Chicago applies to licensed vehicles,
and motor scooters are not licensed.
Commissioner Murphy asked whether the ordinance proposes confiscating motor scooters.
Deputy Chief Folliard replied in the negative, and noted that there is a fine structure under section five.
Commissioner Collins asked whether the Sheriffs Office has lobbied for state regulation.

1860

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

Deputy Chief Folliard replied in the negative.
First Deputy Chief of Police Eddie McCann, Jr., Forest Preserve District, Cook County stated that on
behalf of Chief Waszak, they are one hundred percent for the ordinance, especially regarding Forest
Preserve bike paths, roads and trails. The only motor driven vehicles the Forest Preserve deems
appropriate are Forest Preserve police vehicles in case of emergency. Bird watchers, horseback riders and
children are put at risk by motorized scooters.
Commissioner Steele asked whether there is any place in the Forest Preserve where motor scooters can be
operated.
First Deputy Chief of Police McCann replied in the negative; their aim is too keep the Forest Preserve as
people friendly as possible.
Commissioner Maldonado asked whether motor scooters are at present allowed on Forest Preserve
premises.
First Deputy Chief of Police McCann replied in the negative.
Commissioner Maldonado asked under what authority or ordinance are motor scooters prohibited in the
Forest Preserve.
Chainnan Hansen replied that he believes there is a Forest Preserve ordinance banning them.
Commissioner Maldonado made a distinction between the trails and the paved areas at the Forest
Preserve.
First Deputy Chief of Police McCann made the distinction that unlicensed motor vehicles cannot be
driven on Forest Preserve property.
Mr. Beligratis, State's Attorney 's Office, replied that special districts are given their own legislative
authority; this proposed ordinance covers special districts because the vehicle code does not reach special
district areas. He was uncertain whether there is a Forest Preserve code that covers unlicensed motorized
vehicles.
First Deputy Chief of Police McCann noted that the Forest Preserve District does issue tickets to motor
scooter riders who traverse the parking lots.
Commissioner Maldonado clarified that if the Forest Preserve District has no ordinance in place
prohibiting motor scooters that this be presented to the Board so that it can write the prohibition into an
ordinance.
Commissioner Suffredin noted that there is an ordinance: Section 4-1-Sa ofthe Forest Preserve Code " It
is unlawful for the operation of an automobile, motorcycle, motor scooter, or other motor vehicle to drive
upon or cause to be driven upon such motor vehicle through any woodland or upon any walk, sidewalk,
trail, path, whether marked or unmarked, within the property of the Forest Preserve District." He stated
that it went on to say, " nor upon any road or drive, or parking space within said district, except in the
manner in according to regulations prescribed by the District' s Board of Commissioners."

1861

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

Commissioner Suffredin asked whether there are incident reports concerning motor scooter accidents
within the last six to twelve months. He requested that First Deputy Chief of Police McCann get such
information to the Board before next week's vote on the ordinance.
Wally Kos, Superintendent, Highway Department stated that he would encourage a transitional period to
inform the municipalities and townships of the pending ordinance. He also referenced Senate Bill 2104
introduced by Senator DeLeo in October of last year. The bill was referred to the Rules Committee in the
fall and then went to the Transportation Committee and then was referred in February back to the Rules
Committee. The bill has gone nowhere, and there is not expected to be any state legislation this year.
Commissioner Gornrnn clarified the distinction between Vespas/motorcycles and motorized scooters.
Commissioner Collins asked whether the DeLeo state bill ever made it out of committee.
Superintendent Kos replied in the negative.
Commissioner Collins asked whether motor scooters were included.
Superintendent Kos replied that the definition referred to upright scooters.
Chairman Hansen asked Superintendent Kos for a copy of the bill.
Superintendent Kos agreed to supply a copy of the bill to the Chairman.
Mr. Beligratis, noted that the amendment could be amended, for example three or six months, or warnings
could be given for an initial period of time instead of actually enforcing the ordinance immediately.
Commissioner Suffredin suggested that the committee examine a Forest Preserve ordinance that was
passed last year that required bike helmets for children. A section of the ordinance contains a one year
educational period and details the education and initial enforcement.
Commissioner Murphy stated that it would be preferable to not issue tickets until a later date, but to issue
warnings effective immediately, to optim ize the public's safety.
Commissioner Daley stated that it would be necessary to include language to the effect that violations
would be waived until six months after the passage of the ordinance.
Commissioner Gonnan asked whether the Forest Preserve ordinance requires motor scooter riders to wear
helmets.
Commissioner Suffredin replied in the negative.
Commissioner Hansen asked Mr. Beligratis to go through the ordinance for the edification of the
commissioners and asked him and Commissioner Suffredin to put forward language for section six of the
ordinance relating to an educational period.
Commissioner Murphy suggested the following language: "This ordinance shall be in full force and effect
from and after its approval by the Board of Commissioners, however, citations will not be issued until six
months hence or whatever date is chosen."

1862

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004
Mr. Beligratis suggested the following language: "It will be in full force and effect 180 days after its
approval by the Board." He stated this will circumvent the issue of not issuing citations. He cautioned
however, that it would be necessary to give adequate notice to the public that it will become enforced
beginning upon the effective date.
Commissioner Murphy made the point that the earlier the ordinance goes into effect, the earlier the public
is safe.
Chainnan Hansen stated that it might be possible to satisfy both concerns of notification and safety by
making the warning period 90 days, and somewhere in the "whereas" section mandate that law
enforcement agencies infonn all appropriate governmental units of the ordinance provisions.
Commissioner Murphy noted that Commissioner Maldonado suggested an addendum to her suggestion
that warnings be issued for an initial period; warnings would serve to educate.
Commissioner Steele suggested that the language indicate that verbal warnings will be issued, to save the
County the expense of written tickets.
Chairman Hansen suggested the following language: This ordinance shall be in full force and effect 90
days after its approval by the Board of Commissioners. From the date of approval for 90 days warnings
shall be issued by Jaw enforcement entities.
Commissioner Daley noted that the Deputy Chief of Patrol from the Sheriff's Office indicated that 6
months would be required.
Commissioner Murphy stated that she prefers a written warning, even something pre-printed, to a verbal
warning; preferably one that indicates that the second time they are stopped or after a given date they will
receive a ticket.
Chainnan Hansen noted some Forest Preserve language submitted by Commissioner Suffredin, which
includes "enforcement shall begin on." He noted that there should be an educational period of six
months. He stated that the language for section six should be made available to the Board at the time of
proceedings on June 15th.
Commissioner Daley asked for a definition under Section 1.
Commissioner Hansen suggested that the meeting be continued until next Tuesday when the committee
meets again and at that point pass the ordinance with amendments to Sections I and 6.
Commissioner Gorman asked whether Vespas and mopeds need to be exempted.
Chainnan Hansen replied in the negative.
Mr. Beligratis noted that licensed vehicles are not allowed on sidewalks.
Commissioner Gorman asked whether all municipalities are covered.
Mr. Beligratis replied in the affinnative, unless they pass their own ordinances.
Commissioner Murphy asked whether a municipality could pass an ordinance not to adopt Cook County's
ordinance.

1863

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

Mr. Beligratis replied in the positive.
Commissioner Butler noted that the law could become confusing between municipalities.
Commissioner Collins asked who has j urisdiction, municipalities or the County.
Mr. Beligratis replied the municipalities have jurisdiction; however if there is no local ordinance, the
County ' s would apply; the ordinance would apply in unincorporated Cook County and in special districts.
Chainnan Hansen asked for an answer on this question by the next meeting.
Commissioner Butler asked what effect the ordinance would have on the City of Chicago.
Mr. Beligratis stated that the City of Chicago passed Ordinance Number 356020 which allows anyone age
sixteen and over to operate motorized scooters; thi s ordinance takes precedence over the County's
ordinance.
Chainnan Hansen stated that with regards to police powers, according to Home Rule powers, municipal
ordinances supercede the County's unless there is special legi slation; the County's Home Rule powers
cannot even supercede a municipality that is not home ruled.
Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved to defer Communication No.
265630. The motion carried.
Commissioner Steele moved to adjourn. Seconded by Commissioner Butler, the motion carried
and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfull y submitted,
COMMITTEE ON ROADS AND BRIDGES
CARL R. HANSEN, Chainnan
ATTEST: MICHELLE HARRIS, Secretary
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Report of the Committee on
Roads and Bridges be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Commissioner Daley asked whether the new language would conflict with the State's ordinances?

vehicle code.

areas directly and to any incorporated areas that do not have local legislation?
Mr. Beligratis stated our ordinance could apply to unincorporated areas within Cook County and to those
municipalities that had not enacted ordinances on this subject. Any municipality home rule or otherwise
whose ordinance conflicts with ours would supercede ours.

265924

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT, by Gwendolyn D. Clemons,
Director, transmitting a Communication, dated May 14, 2004:
Re:

J & L CNC Quality Machining, Inc.
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfuJly submitting this Resolution regarding the Company's application for Class 6b
property tax incentive for your consideration.

1912

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

J & L CNC Quality Machining, Inc. requests approval of the special exception to the 24
month abandonment rule under the Class 6b Ordinance. This resolution is required so that
the company can complete its application to the Assessor of Cook County within the 90 day
period from purchase of the property will occurred on June 4, 2004.
Submitting the company's app lication for C lass 6b, the Resolution of the Village of Alsip,
Illinois, and a Department of Planning and Development staff report for your information.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property
Assessment Classification 6b which provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level
for an industrial facility; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application
from J & L CNC Quality Machining, Inc. and the Resolution from the Village of Alsip for an
abandoned industrial facility located at 12633 Springfield, Alsip, Cook County, lllinois,
Property Index Numbers 24-26-300-090-0000 and 24-26-300-093-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of
qualifying abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less
than 24 consecutive months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was
abandoned for 23 months at the time of application and that special circumstances are
present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners
of the County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners
indicate their approval for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate
Classification 6b abatement incentive to J & L CNC Quality Machining, Inc. for an
abandoned industrial faci lity located at 12633 Springfield, Alsip, Cook County, lllinois,
under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to
forward a certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
*Referred to the Business & Economic Development Committee on 6/3/04.

265915

OFFICE OF CAP ITAL PLANNING AND POLICY by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 10, 2004:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for the Department of Corrections Division VIII RTU (Residential
Treatment Unit) Renovation. It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve
this request.
This project is to replace nine existing air conditioning units, connect them to the campus
chilled water loop and add exhaust fans to existing shower rooms in the wards. The current
building's existing air conditioners and exhaust fans are outdated and inefficient, which
affects the comfort level of the residents and staff and pose numerous problems for the
maintenance personnel.
Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6/3/04.
265916

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 10, 2004:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for tl1e Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids the Department of Community Supervision and Intervention
(DCSI) South Campus Building #3 HY AC System. It is respectfully requested that this
Honorable Body approve this request.
Several floors of Building #3 do not have forced air ventilation. This project provides for the
installation of an air conditioning and ventilation system for the second, third and fourth
floors of Building #3 of DCSI. The new system will consist of a 170-ton chiller and a 40,230
CFM air handler. Vertical supply and return ducts will provide conditioned air to each floor.
Bond Issue ( 19000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6/3/04.

265918

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 10, 2004:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is Change Order No. 4, payable to GF Structures
Corporation, for the Rockwell Warehouse Phase II Interior Project. This change order is for
work necessary to complete the project. It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body
approve this request.
This change order will provide for the following work to be completed:
1.

Wire needed to extend the riser cabling from the basement to the new location of the
main switchboard on the 1st floor.

2.

Addition of new electrical receptacles to the 3rd, 4th and 5th floors. The receptacles
must be located on dedicated circuits and wired back to the branch circuit panels in
order for the user agency to operate oscillating fans they use during the summer months
in the warehouse areas.

3.

Relocate vent and water piping to the 4th floor washroom. The vent and water piping
needed to be routed back to its original location in order for the renovated bathroom to
be operational.

4.

Provide a door for access to a storage room.

5.

Install control valves and replacement of steam traps in the elevator penthouses.

A 66 day time extension is requested by GF Structures Corporation to complete this work.

Commissioner Hansen inquired about the plumbing work at Division I.
Michael E. LaMont, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy, stated eight years ago extensive
plumbing work was done at Division I. The work being described is not part of the scope. The work
being described is putting fixtures on existing risers behind the walls. This work was not included in the
previous scope.

Mr. LaMont stated the square footage is one-hundred-seventy-thousand and this number includes four
floors and the basement.

maintenance.
Mr. LaMont stated the Medical District, Rush and University of Illinois were not interested in
participating in the capitol cost. Rush Hospital and University of Illinois Hospital should pay a landing
fee for the use of the helipad.

RESOLUTIONS
04-R-222
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE CARL R. HANSEN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, on June 5, 2004, Ronald Reagan, the 40th President of the United States, was called from
our midst at the age of 93; and
WHEREAS, Ronald Reagan was born in Tampico, Illinois on February 6, 1911 , and moved to Dixon,
Illinois when he was nine, where he starred in high school football, taught Sunday school, and was a
lifeguard. He graduated from Eureka College in 1932; and
WHEREAS, Ronald Reagan learned the importance of compassion for people as a result of growing up
during the Depression in the hard-hit Midwest, and he assumed responsibility at an early age in order to
support his fami ly; and

1920

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDJNGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

WHEREAS, Ronald Reagan pursued a successful career in broadcasting in the Midwest, followed by a
career in Hollywood during which he made over fifty movies and served as head of the Screen Actors
Guild; and

WHEREAS, Ronald Reagan served his country during difficult times in his two consecutive terms as
Governor of California from 1967 to 1975, and then as President of the United States from 1981 to 1989;
and

WHEREAS, Ronald Reagan's optimism, character, and ability to communicate helped to restore the
confidence of Americans in their country; and

WHEREAS, President Reagan's principled opposition to Communism undoubtedly hastened the demise
of the repressive and dangerous regime that was the Soviet Union, and helped to eventually end the
division of continental Europe, and to bring " peace through strength" by winni ng the Cold War; and

WHEREAS, when President Reagan took office, the U.S. economy was beset by historically high
interest rates, high inflation and a rise in the unemployment rate to double digits. However, by the end of
President Reagan 's second tenn in 1989, 16 million jobs had been created while inflation was reduced;
and

WHEREAS, upon learning that he had Alzheimer' s disease in 1993, Ronald Reagan gracefully exited
public life just as he had handled his previous bouts of illness and injury, by writing an open letter to the
American people in which his optimism for America remained undim inished, when he said, " I know that
for America there will always be a bright dawn ahead."

NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its sorrow at the passing of President Ronald Reagan, and extends its deepest sympathy to
the fami ly of this great man, a man whose optimism, energy, and inte lligence restored Americans' vision
of the United States of America as "that shining city on a hill."

Approved and adopted this 15th day of June 2004.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Gonnan, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. President Stroger called for a rising vote. The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

04-R-223
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO AND ROBERTO MALDONADO
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Vicente Fox Quesada first ran for public office in 1988 and was elected to Congress
representing the 3rd district in Leon, Guanajuato, then in 1995 he was elected governor of Guanajuato; he
won the Presidential elections of 2000, representing the "Alliance for Change" comprised of two political
parties, the PAN and PVEM; and
WHEREAS, Vicente Fox Quesada is visiting the United States for a three-day, three-state visit, his
second visit to the U.S. as President of Mexico and his third as an elected official; and
WHEREAS, he will arrive on June 16, 2004 to Chicago to inaugurate the new offices of The Consulate
General of Mexico located at 204 South Ashland Avenue, thus keeping his word when in 2001 he
promised to build a bigger and more efficient Consulate to the Mexican community; and
WHEREAS, the offices of The Consulate General of Mexico in Chicago are the largest in the world, the
only new offices built during his presidency, and they where completely financed by the Mexican
government at a cost of nearly eight million dollars; and
WHEREAS, on June 17, 2004 he will visit the installations of Unity Middle High School in Cicero and
will meet privately with elected officials of Hispanic origin to discuss and emphasize the need of
strategies in educating children of Mexican origin, to better their school life and future opportunities; and
WHEREAS , he wants to promote the interests of the Mexican community in the Midwest, knowing that
the Chicago metropolitan area holds the largest percentage of residents of Mexican origin in Illinois; and
WHEREAS, his visit to the United States will continue with a visit to Michigan on June 17, 2004 and
will end in Minnesota on June 18, 2004; and
WHEREAS, he will be accompanied by his wife, Marta Sahagun; the Secretary of Education, Reyes
Tamez; the Secretary of Foreign Relations, Luis Ernesto Derbez; and the Dean of the National
Autonomous University of Mexico (UNAM), Juan Ramon de la Fuente.

1922

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Members of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners do hereby extend a wann welcome to the President of Mexico, Vicente Fox
Quesada, his wife and members of the cabinet that accompany him to this visit to the United States; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable

AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Commemorating the lOOth Anniversary of Holy Rosary Parish
WHEREAS, Holy Rosary Parish opened in 1904 to serve the Italian immigrant population of Chicago's
Near West Side; and
WHEREAS, Holy Rosary has, over the years, served admirably many Italian parishioners and welcomed
new Hispanic faithful to the congregation; and
WHEREAS, Holy Rosary reaches out to former parishioners by holding homecoming masses several
times a year; and

1923

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

WHEREAS, Holy Rosary Parish operated an elementary school, administered by the Sisters of Mercy
until the late 1970s, graduating many young men and women who have later succeeded in a variety of
fields; and
WHEREAS, to celebrate the remarkable history of this parish while ensuring its future vitality, Holy
Rosary Church will host an anniversary banquet on July 10, 2004, exactly 100 years after the church was
dedicated; and
WHEREAS, current parishioner Frank Belcastro and fonner parishioner Dolores Paccagnini Garro will
be honored at the banquet; and
WHEREAS, the anniversary celebration will be spearheaded by Bishop Lawrence Sabatini, C.S, pastor
of Holy Rosary and champion of the parish's revival; and
WHEREAS, Holy Rosary had fallen into disrepair, but is now rehabilitated and poised to embark on its
next hundred years.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook do hereby congratulate Bishop Sabatini and all past and present parishioners of Holy
Rosary Parish on this lOOth anniversary.

Approved and adopted this 15th day of June 2004.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

1924

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

WHEREAS, Officer Freeman has demonstrated his commitment to law enforcement, the Chicago Police
Department, and the residents of Chicago by serving 40 years on the police force; and
WHEREAS, Officer Freeman completed his field training in the 11th Police District and was assigned to
the 13th Police District; and
WHEREAS, Officer Freeman conducted Foot Patrol in the Henry Homer Homes in 1968, during a
turbulent time in our country's history; and
WHEREAS, Officer Freeman has made it home to his family at the end of every shift for last forty years;
and
WHEREAS, Officer Freeman has received numerous accolades for his service, including several
commendations from the Chicago Police Department, Letters of Compliments from citizens of Chicago,
the Public Service Award from the Junior Chamber of Commerce, Community Service Award from
Pilgrim Rest Church and the SPSA Superior Service Award; and
WHEREAS, he has also received many honorable mentions from the Chicago Police Department for
apprehending criminals and solving crimes; and
WHEREAS, Officer Freeman has contributed significantly to busting up street gangs; and
WHEREAS, Officer Freeman has mentored numerous young men to provide them alternatives to joining
gangs; and
WHEREAS, he has made personal investment in Chicago communities and residents to create safer
streets, schools and neighborhoods.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Board of
Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, do hereby extend to
Officer William D. Freeman our sincerest congratulations on his retirement. This Honorable Body and
the people of Cook County celebrate your 40 years of committed service to the Chicago Police
Department; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that a copy of same be tendered to Officer William D. Freeman
memorializing his exemplary law enforcement career.

RESOLUTION

AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

WHEREAS, American Legion Post 194 1 of 900 South La Grange Road will hold their 60th anniversary
on Saturday, June 19, 2004; and
WHEREAS, the Post Number 1941 designates the year when the United States entered the war; and
WHEREAS, Post Number 1941 was founded under the guidance of La Grange Post 41 for the growing
number of veterans returning home after World War II; and
WHEREAS, Post Number 1941 has grown from the fifteen original members who started the post to
over 600 members today; and
WHEREAS, the post name of Robert E. Coulter, Jr. was selected as a tribute to U.S. Anny Air Corps
Maj or Robert E. Coulter, Jr. who was the son of Mr. and Mrs. Robert E. Coulter of La Grange, who died
in action as a pilot of a Flying Fortress over North Africa in 1943; and

1928

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

WHEREAS, Robert E. Coulter, Jr. was the first La Grange resident to lose his life for his country and his
portrait is displayed in his honor at the post home; and
WHEREAS, Post 1941 actively sponsors many scout troops, school bands, baseball teams and many
other community projects; and
WHEREAS, Post 1941 has provided scholarships to local area high school seniors to further their
education and sponsored Boy Scout Troop 19; and
WHEREAS, members of Post 1941 have provided many services to others and shown outstanding
compassion to the hospitalized veterans with frequent visits and gifts.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body, and an official copy be tendered to the Commander of Robert E. Coulter Post 1941 ,
Larry Jaderberg, commemorating its 60th anniversary on June 19, 2004.
Approved and adopted this 15th day of June 2004.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. T he motion carried unanimously.

THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER

ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
In Memory of Kenneth A. Whitney

WHEREAS, Kenneth Arthur Whitney died on June 4, 2004; and

1929

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 15, 2004

WHEREAS, Kenneth A. Whitney was a devoted husband to Eleanor, with whom he shared 34 years of
marriage, and father to sons Ryan and Scott; and
WHEREAS, throughout his life, Kenneth A. Whitney cherished his family and valued the time he was
able to spend with his mother Lumetta Whitney, brothers Timothy, John and Thomas and their families,
his sister Barbara, his father Timothy Eric Whitney, Sr. and brother Raymond who proceeded him in
death; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Whitney, known as Ken to his family, friends and colleagues, was a man of great
compassion and conviction who time and again stood up for the issues he believed in and always
endeavored to share his experiences and knowledge with others; and
WHEREAS, a life long advocate of social justice issues, Ken Whitney was particularly interested in
education issues and was known as an outspoken advocate for quality education in racially balanced
settings; and
WHEREAS, Ken Whitney was proud to call Evanston home for 28 years and had a great interest in the
civic and cultural affairs of the City, including his tenure from 1991 to 1995 on the District 65 School
Board, during which he also served for a time as its president; and
WHEREAS, admitted to the Illinois Bar in 1972, Ken Whitney had a distinguished law career which
included serving as Chief Counsel for the Department of General Services for the State of Illinois during
the Walker Administration and for 23 years, he served as the in-house legal counsel for Motorola; and
WHEREAS, Ken strongly believed in giving back to his community; he freely gave of his time and
resources to numerous boards and organizations including Kappa Alpha Psi Fraternity, Inc., of which he
was a lifetime member, and the NAACP North Shore Chapter; he was also the founder of the Evanston
African American Research Group and a founding board member of Shorefront journal; and
WHEREAS, Ken Whitney was loved and respected by his friends and colleagues whose lives he
touched.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of
Kenneth A. Whitney and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of
Kenneth A. Whitney so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 15th day of June 2004.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
